‘рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реБрдХреНрдереЗ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрдпреГрдЪрдВ рд╕рдкреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН ред рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рдордгрд┐рдХрд╛тАУ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реБрдХреНрдереЗ рджреНрд╡реНрдпрдзрд┐рдХрд╛ рдордиреБрд░реНрд╡реИрд╡рд╕реНрд╡рддреЛ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рдВ рд╣ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЧрд╛рдердореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡рд┐рд╡рд╕реНрд╡рддрдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░реЛ рдордиреБрд░реНрдЛрд╖рд┐рдГред рдкреНрд░рдердорд╛рддреГрддреАрдпрд╛рджреНрдпрдпреБрдЬреЛ рдмреГрд╣рддреНрдпреЛ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрд╛рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдерд╛рджрд┐рдпреБрдЬрдГ рд╕рддреЛрдмреГрд╣рддреНрдпрдГ ред рдЗрджрдорд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдВ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдгрд╛рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ ред рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рд▓реИрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдХрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

27 (647)
All Gods
Manu Vaivasvata
22 verses: br╠еhat─л alternating with satobr╠еhat─л, arranged in prag─Бthas
This hymn to the All Gods falls roughly into three parts on the basis of the gods addressed. The first eight verses contain a number of named gods, whose associa tions seem random, rather than ordered into the usual functional groupsтАФwith, for example, the Maruts mentioned next to the ─Аdityas, singly or jointly, or to Agni. In contrast to this jumble of divine names, the middle section (vss. 9тАУ14) mentions no gods except Savitar (vs. 12), and he is in service of the unnamed plural тАЬyouтАЭ used of the gods as a corporate entity. The unity and superimposability of the vari ous gods in this section is made clear in verses 13тАУ14. The final section (vss. 15тАУ22) mentions only the ─Аdityas, though in fact they appear only in verses 15, 17, and 22.
Despite these differences in divine address, the hymn is unified by its concerns, especially the desire for protection and shelter offered by the gods (see, e.g., vss. 4, 9, 20), and by its vocabularyтАФin particular the epithet vi┼Ыv├б-vedas тАЬaffording all possessionsтАЭ (vss. 2, 4, 11, 19, 20, 21) or, according to others, тАЬhaving all knowledge, which is a near phonological match to v├н┼Ыve dev─Б╠Бс╕е тАЬAll Gods,тАЭ to whom the hymn is dedicated. The ritual context is also very much present in the hymn.
On the basis of verse 12 and the sketch of SavitarтАЩs functions there, Geldner suggests that this is an evening hymn. But later in the hymn the poet insistently mentions various times of day (vss. 19тАУ21), and so it seems rather that he is seeking the aid and protection of the gods round-the-clock, as it were.

The language of the hymn is fairly simple and straightforward, and the lexicon often repetitive. But the effect is pleasing, and the poem hardly deserves RenouтАЩs judgment (EVP IV: 106) that it is тАЬbanalтАЭ and тАЬfacile.тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni is the Purohita at the sacrifice; the stones, the sacred grass (are prepared) for the ceremony. Iinvoke with the holy verse the Maruts, Brahmaс╣Зaspati, and all the gods, for their desirable protection.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Purohita= plural ced in front, (or on the east), on the uttara vedi

Jamison Brereton

Agni has been set in front while the solemn speech (is being recited), as have the pressing stones and the ritual grass while the ceremony (is
going forth).
With a verse I implore the Maruts, Brahmaс╣Зaspati, and the gods for help worthy to be chosen.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take both ukth├й and adhvar├й as functional loc. absolutes. Cf. ┼Ыasy├бm─Бna ukth├й (VI.23.1, also IV.20.10, X.45.10), prayaty ├бdhvar├й (I.16.3 [=VIII.3.5], V.28.6 [=VIII.71.12], etc.). The latter expression appears as a full phrase in 3a pr├б s├║ na etv adhvar├бс╕е.

Griffith

CHEIF Priest is Agni at the laud, as stones and grass at sacrifice:
With song I seek the Maruts, Brahmanaspati, Gods for help much to be desired.

Geldner

Agni ist zum Leiter des Lobliedes bestellt, die Pre├Яsteine, das Barhis zum Leiter der Opferhandlung. In gebundner Rede wende ich mich an die Marut, an Brihaspati, an die G├╢tter um ihre vielbegehrte Gunst.

Grassmann

Dem Spruch ist Agni vorgesetzt, dem Opfer Steine und die Streu; Ich geh mit Lied die Maruts, den Gebetes Herrn, um sch├╢nen Schutz die G├╢tter an.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou come (Agni) to the victim, to the dwelling (of the worshipper), to the touchwood, to the Soma, atdawn and at night; universal deities, givers of wealth, knowing all things, be the defenders of our pious actс╣гтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Dwelling of the worshipper: pс╣Ыthiv─лm = idam devasadanam, this chamber of the gods;

Oс╣гadhiс╕е = may alsoimply, annual plural nts; uс╣г─Бs─Б naktam oс╣гadhiс╕е = you come to dawn and might (these being the times for theoffering), and the Soma-grinding stones;

Vasavaс╕е = v─Бsayit─Бraс╕е, causers of habitations

Jamison Brereton

Here I have sung the (sacrificial) animal, the earth, the trees, Dawn and Night, the plants.
And do you all, good ones affording all possessions, become furtherers of our poetic insights.

Jamison Brereton Notes

uс╣г─Б╠Бs─Б n├бktam is a curious variant of the dual dvandva uс╣г─Б╠Бs─Б-n├бkt─Б, occurring only here. Oldenberg suggests that it is an ex. of a singular 2nd member following a dual in the 1st (cf. AiG II.1.154), which seems a description not an explanation. I think two factors entered into its creation: on the one hand, all forms of uс╣г─Б╠Бs─Б-n├бkt─Б precede a consonant; here that form would be in hiatus with vowel-initial ├│с╣гadh─лс╕е.

(Acdg. to Oldenberg, BR think that the original form was in fact n├бkt─Б, but it was altered to avoid hiatus.) But all forms of uс╣г─Б╠Бs─Б-n├бkt─Б are also initial in trimeter verse, where a heavy fifth syllable is fine. This is dimeter verse, and a heavy fifth syllable would produce a bad cadence; light -am V╠Дallows an iambic cadence.

Here and elsewhere through the hymn I render vi┼Ыv├бvedas- as тАШaffording all possessionsтАЩ, not тАШpossessing all knowledgeтАЩ, because it is usually found in the context of the godsтАЩ generosity.

Griffith

I sing to cattle and to Earth, to trees, to Dawns, to Night, to plants.
O all ye Vasus, ye possessors of all wealth, be ye the furtherers of our thoughts.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the universal deities, possessors of all opulence, destroyers of foes, be (near) to Manu for hisprosperity; do you, who know all things, secure to us an abode safe from robbers through unassailableprotections.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Safe from robbers: avс╣Ыkam stenarahitam = free from any annoyances, b─Бdh─Бrahitam

Jamison Brereton

For they all, affording all possessions, caring for the stranger, will be there for Manu, to increase him.
With invulnerable protectors, you who afford all possessionsтАФhold out to us shelter that keeps the wolf away.

Griffith

Lords of all wealth, may they be strengtheners of man, destroyers of his enemies.
Lords of all wealth, do ye, with guards which none may harm, preserve our dwelling free from foes.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDirect, Maruts, your beloved horses (to our rite); Mitra, (come to our) oblations; and may Indra, andVaruс╣Зa, and the swift leaders, the ─Аdityas, sit down on our sacred grass.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Dear are those equine (gifts) of yours and dear to you the oblations to which you drive, o Maruts and Mitra.
Let Indra, Varuс╣Зa, the powerful men [=Maruts?], (and?) the ─Аdityas sit on this ritual grass of ours.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The syntax of ab is oddly muddled for what seems on the surface a banal sentiment. The problem is the position of the relative and its relationship both to the priy─Б╠Бearlier in the verse and accented verb pray─Бth├бna later. The key, I think, is neut.

pl. ├б┼Ыvy─Б тАШequineтАЩ. Contra Geldner I donтАЩt think that it should be construed with havy─Б╠Б, with тАЬequine oblationsтАЭ as a reference to the A┼Ыvamedha – an interpr. that Renou rightly calls тАЬadventurous.тАЭ The stem ├б┼Ыvya-, esp. in the neut. pl., is generally used of gifts (r─Б╠Бdhas-, magh├б-) consisting of horses that gods (or patrons) give to mortals (e.g., VII.16.10 y├й r─Б╠Бdh─Бс╣Гsi d├бdaty ├б┼Ыvy─Б magh─Б╠Б), whereas havy─Б╠Бare of course oblations given by mortals to gods. I think we therefore must reckon with two different constructions in this hemistich, which accounts for the fractured word order.

On the one hand I see a nominal clause (or rather a nominal clause whose subject is itself a relative clause): тАЬwhich equine gifts are yours (i.e., come from you), (they) are dear (to us).тАЭ On the other, the same predicate priy─Б╠Бhas as subject a full rel.

clause whose verb is pray─Бth├бna: тАЬwhich oblations you drive to, (they) are dear to you.тАЭ The vaс╕е is used both as a genitive (in the first construction) and as a dative (in the second). Unfortunately it is wrongly placed in the relative clause for this second interpr., but I can only imagine that the poet allowed this small breach to avoid doubling the vaс╕е, or rather that the dative could be integrated into the rel. cl.: тАЬwhich oblations for you you drive to, they are dear.тАЭ Note that two different entities are dear to two different groups of beings. I have not yet solved the problem of abh├н, however. RenouтАЩs interpr. requires pr├б тИЪy─Б to be transitive and also intermingles the main and relative clauses in an illegitimate way and should be rejected: тАЬDi(riger) vers (nos) oblations les ch├иres troupes de chevaux que vous mettez en marche.тАЭ Geldner takes tur─Б╠Бn├бraс╕е as a qualifier of the immediately following ─Аdityas.

Although both tur├б- and nс╣Ы╠Б- can sometimes apply to the ─Аdityas, they are more frequently used of the Maruts, who are somewhat dominant in this part of the hymn (1c, 3d, 5c, 6a, 8a).

Griffith

Send us delightful things, ye Maruts, on your steeds: come ye, O Mitra, to our gifts.
Let Indra, Varuna, and the Adityas sit, swift Heroes, on our sacred grass.

English translation:

тАЬBearing the clipped sacred grass, offering in due order the (sacrificial) food, presenting the effusedSoma, and having the fires kindled, we invoke you, Varuс╣Зa, (and the rest), as did Manus.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Varuс╣Зa: when Mitraand Varuс╣Зa are named singly, both are intended, and sometimes even more of the Vi┼Ыvadevas; cf. ┼ЪathapathaBr─Бhmaс╣Зa 1.8.1, Manu’s sacrifice

Jamison Brereton

We who have ritual grass twisted for you and pleasurable offerings set out in due order,
who have soma pressed and the fire kindled, like Manu, invoke (you), o Varuс╣Зa.

Griffith

We who have trimmed the grass for you, and set the banquet in array,
And pressed the Soma, call you, Varuina, like men, with sacrificial fires aflame.

Geldner

Wir rufen euch, nachdem wir ordnungsgem├д├Я das Barhis herumgelegt, die Opfer-gen├╝sse bereitet, Soma ausgepre├Яt haben, o Varuna, wie Manu tat, bei entz├╝ndetem Feuer.

Grassmann

Wir rufen euch der Reihe nach, die Streu und Opfer wir besorgt, Den Somatrank gebraut und Agni’s Glut entflammt, nach Menschen Art, o Varuna.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

English translation:

тАЬDeities, possessed of all wealth, I, desirous of offering worship, address to you verily unprecedentedpraise, for the sake of obtaining desired affluence.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Because just now (I have dispatched) a praise invocation to you, just now for the distribution of desirable goodsтАФ
to you who afford all possessions have I, doing homage, dispatched (it) like a lead(-cow).

Griffith

For now have I sent forth to you, that I may win a fair reward,
Lords of all wealth, with homage, this my song of praise. like a milch-cow that faileth not.

Geldner

Denn jetzt habe ich an euch ein Preislied, jetzt um Anteil an dem Gut zu erlangen, ehrerbietig losgelassen, ihr Allwissende, wie eine zweite Kuh zum Kalb.

Grassmann

Denn hier hab’ ich ergossen euch das Lob, um Sch├╢nes zu empfahn, Vor euch mich beugend, o die ihr allwissend seid, wie einen Strom, der nie versiegt.

English translation:

тАЬDevoutly praised (Maruts), when the adorable Savit─Б has risen above you, then bipeds andquadrupeds, and the flying birds, seeking (their objects), enter (upon their functions).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O you of good guidance, for you has this Savitar, worthy to be chosen, stood up, erect.
Down have settled the busy two-footed and four-footed, and those that fly about.

Griffith

Excellent Savitar hath mounted up on high for you, ye sure and careful Guides.
Bipeds and quadrupeds, with several hopes and aims, and birds have settled to their tasks.

English translation:

тАЬMay the universal gods with one consent be together the givers (of riches) to Manu; may they, bothtoday and hereafter, be the bestowers of wealth upon us and upon our posterity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For the gods, all as one, are of like fervor for Manu, of like generosity. Let them be for us now, let them be in the future for our progeny, the finders of a wide realm.

Griffith

For of one spirit are the Gods with mortal man, co-sharers all of gracious gifts.
May they increase our strength hereafter and to-day, providing case and ample room.

English translation:

тАЬI glorify you, inoxious deities, in the plural ce of praises; no harm befalls the man who, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa,offers (oblations) to your glories.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I recite to you, o you without deceit, at the concourse of praise invocations. No injury (comes) to that mortal who has done honor to your
ordinances, o Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, (and Aryaman).

Jamison Brereton Notes

I assume that Aryaman is tacitly included with Mitra and Varuс╣Зa in c, given the vaс╕е in d (and a). In the phrase varuс╣Зa mitra m├бrti yam, trisyllabic m├бrti yam is a sort of scrambling of Aryaman.

On the apparent bad cadence produced by ├бvidhat, see remarks ad II.1.7, where ArnoldтАЩs suggestion to read a long augment is adopted.

Griffith

I laud you, O ye Guileless Gods, here where we meet to render praise.
None, Varuna and Mitra, harins the mortal, man who honours and obeys your laws.

Geldner

Ich preise euch, ihr Truglosen, im Wettstreit der Loblieder. Nicht trifft den Sterblichen die Hinterlist, Mitra und Varuna, der euren Personen gehuldigt hat.

Grassmann

Euch, holdgesinnte, preise ich in dieser Lieder Chorgesang; Nicht trifft, o Mitra-Varuna, Verletzung den, der euren Satzungen gehorcht.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe enlarges his dweling, he has abundant food who offers you (oblations) to obtain a blessing; throughhis pious acts he is born on every side in his children; all prosper (through your favour) unharmed (by enemies).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He furthers his dwelling place, ex(tends) his great refreshments, who does ritual service to your liking.
He is propagated through progeny forth from his foundation.
Unharmed and whole, he thrives.

Jamison Brereton Notes

pr├б praj─Б╠Бbhir j─Бyate is a nice figure in which pr├б doubles the first part of the cmpd. and j─Бyate the second.

dh├бrmaс╣Зas p├бri receives quite varied interpr. I take it as a spatial metaphor: the fortunate pious man is propagated through his progeny тАЬfrom his foundation,тАЭ that is, starting from himself and spreading out by children and grandchildren (etc.).

Griffith

He makes his house endure, he gathers plenteous food who pays obedience to your will.
Born in his sons anew he spreads as Law commands, and prospers every way unharmed.

Geldner

Der vergr├╢├Яert sein Haus, vermehrt seinen gro├Яen Speisesegen, wer eurem Wunsch entspricht. Er pflanzt sich pflichtgem├д├Я durch Kinder fort, er gedeiht ganz und gar ohne Schaden.

Grassmann

Der mehrt sein Gut und h├дuft sich grosse Nahrung an, wer eurem Willen huldiget, Der pflanzt sich nach der Reihe fort durch Kindeskind, gedeiht vollkommen, unversehrt.

English translation:

тАЬHe gains (wealth) without war, he travels along the roads with quick (horses), whom Aryaman, Mitraand Varuс╣Зa, alike munificent, and acting in concert, protect.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

That one acquires without fighting; along (paths) easy to go on he travels his routes,
whom Mitra, Varuс╣Зa, and Aryaman protectтАФthey of like generosity and like delight.

Griffith

E’en without war he gathers wealth, and goes hisway on pleasant paths,
Whom Mitra, Varuna and Aryaman protect, sharing the gift,of one accord.

Auch ohne Kampf gewinnt er Gut, geht auf gebahnten Pfaden hin, Wen gleich an Huld Arjaman, Mitra, Varuna besch├╝tzen alle im Verein.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рдЕрдЬреНрд░реЗ рдЪрд┐рддреН ред тАШрдЬреНрд░рд┐ рдЕрднрд┐рднрд╡реЗ’ред рдкрд░реИрд░рдирднрд┐рднрд╡рдиреАрдпреЗрд╜рдкрд┐ рдкрд░рдкреБрд░реЗ рдиреНрдпрдЮреНрдЪрдирдВ рдирд┐рддрд░рд╛рдВ рдЧрдордирдореН рдЕрд╕реНрдореИ рдордирд╡реЗ рдХреГрдгреБрде рдпреВрдпрдВ рдХреБрд░реБрдд ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдЕрдЬреНрд░реЗ рдЛрдЬреБрдЧрдордиреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдереЗ рдЧрдордирдВ рдХреБрд╕реНрдд ред рддрдерд╛ рджреБрд░реНрдЧреЗ рдЪрд┐рддреН рдЕрдЧрдиреНрддрд╡реНрдпреЗрд╜рдкрд┐ рд╕реНрдерд▓реЗ рд╕реБрд╕рд░рдгрдореН ред рд╕реГ рдЧрддреМ’ ред рд╢реЛрднрдирдЧрдордирдореН рдЖ рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН рдХреБрд░реБрдд ред рдПрд╡рдВ рд╕рддрд┐ рд╕рд╛ рдПрд╖рд╛ рдЕрд╢рдирд┐рдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рддрджреЗрддрджрд╛рдпреБрдзрдореН рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреЛ рдЧрдиреНрддреБрд░реНрдордиреЛрдГ рдиреБ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдВ рдкрд░рдГ рдкрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рджреНрднрд╡реЗрддреН ред рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рддреН рд╕рд╛ рдЕрд╢рдирд┐рдГ рдЕрд╕реНрд░реЗрдзрдиреНрддреА рдХрд╛рдВрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рджрдкреНрдпрд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рддреА рд╡рд┐ рдирд╢реНрдпрддреБ рд╡рд┐рдирд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рднрд╡реЗрддреН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou enable him (Manu) to proceed by an unobstructed road; you grant him easy access to difficultpasses; may the weapon (of the foe) be far from him, and, inflicting no injury, perish.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Even in the flat plain you make a niche for him; even in difficult going (you make for him) smooth flowing.
Also this missileтАФit is now far from himтАФlet it go unfaltering to
destruction.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The 2nd hemistich presents some niggling syntactic and lexical problems.

To start with the latter, by most interpr. ├бsredhant─л is transitive (Geldner тАЬohne Schaden anzurichten,тАЭ Renou тАЬsans causer de nuisanceтАЭ). But the verb to which this negated participle belongs is consistently intransitive, meaning тАШfailтАЩ, not тАШcause to failтАЩ, and though Grassmann glosses ├бsredhant- (and related stems) as transitive тАШnicht sch├дdigendтАЩ, hence тАШheilsamтАЩ, all passages are compatible with intransitive тАШunfailing, unfalteringтАЩ.

Although in this particular case тАШnot harmingтАЩ might be tempting, the point here must be that the missile should go to destruction without pause or deviation in its trajectory.

I am disturbed by the pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++ p─Бda-final s─Б╠Б, doubling initial eс╣г─Б╠Б, as well as what looks like a self-contained clausette in which it is found: par├│ n├║ s─Б╠Б. Neither Geldner nor Renou takes any notice of the oddly constructed c p─Бda; Geldner takes c and d as independent clauses, while Renou treats cd as a unified clause. My tr. tries to mirror the construction by taking asm─Бt тАж par├│ n├║ s─Б╠Бas a parenthetical. I remain concerned about two things: 1) This is the only passage in which par├бс╕е seems to mean тАШfar fromтАЩ; other passages containing par├бс╕е + ABL. mean тАШbeyond, other thanтАЩ (see also the 1st verse of the next hymn, VIII.28.1, with par├бс╕е тАШbeyondтАЩ without abl.). However, тАШfar from XтАЩ and тАШbeyond XтАЩ are close enough semantically to allay my concerns, and in fact a tr. тАЬit is now beyond himтАЭ would work fine. 2) I do not like the position of asm─Бt, but I must assume that it was extracted from the par├│ n├║ s─Б╠Бclausette in order to conform to the pattern set in p─Бda a: x x cid asmai matched by c: x x cid asm─Бt.

I have reluctantly rendered cid in c as тАШalsoтАЩ (so also Geldner), though it does not match the two cids in a and b (тАШevenтАЩ) because I cannot make тАШevenтАЩ work. (I suppose тАЬeven this missile тАжтАЭ is possible, but it is not favored.)

Griffith

E’en on the plain for him ye make a sloping path, an easy way where road is none:
And far away from him the ineffectual shaft must vanish, shot at him in vain.

Geldner

Auch in der Ebene macht ihr dem einen Schlupfwinkel, auch im Gebirge leichtes Fortkommen. Auch jener Schleuderstein soll weit weg von ihm sein, er soll ohne Schaden anzurichten verschwinden.

Grassmann

Auf ebner Flur auch schafft ihr eine Zuflucht ihm und im Gebirge sch├╢ne Bahn; Das fliegende Geschoss auch sinke fern von ihm zu Boden, nicht ihn sch├дdigend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDivinities of benevolent vigour, since you preside over the rite today, at the rising of the sun, since,possessors of all wealth, (you are present) at his setting, or at his waking, or at the meridian of the day.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Presideover the rite: since you uphold the house (rendered prosperous), gс╣Ыham kaly─Бс╣Зabh┼лtam dh─Бrayatha

Jamison Brereton

Since today as the sun was rising you established truth, o you of dear dominion,
since at (sun)set, at awakening, or since at midday of the day, you
affording all possessions,

Griffith

If ye appoint the rite to-day, kind Rulers, when the Sun ascends,
Lords of all wealth, at sunset or at wakingtime, or be it at the noon of day,

Geldner

Wenn ihr heute bei Sonnenaufgang das Gesetz feststellet, ihr beliebten Herrscher, wenn bei Sonnenuntergang, am Morgen, ihr Allwissende, oder wenn am Mittag,

Grassmann

Wenn ihr bei Sonnenaufgang heut, geliebte Herrscher Gutes schenkt, Beim Untergang, allweise, zur Erwachens Zeit, und in des Tages Mitte auch,

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOr since all-wise deities, you accept the sacrifice, bestowing on the zealous donor (of the oblation) aswelling (such as we may worship in) then, possessors of all wealth, distributors of riches, may we worshp you inthe midst (of that dwelling).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yadv─Бbhipitve asur─Б с╣Ыtam yate chardir yema vid─Бsuс╣гe = yadv─Б asmadyaj├▒amprati yuс╣гm─Бkam abhipr─Бptau yaj├▒am gacchate hav─лс╣Гsi dattavate yajam─Бn─Бya gс╣Ыham prayacchatha,since you give a dwelling to the donor of the oblation proceeding to the rite, which is to bring you to our sacrifice;or, on your approach to our sacrifice

Jamison Brereton

Or since at evening, o lords, you held out shelter to the pious man who pursues truth,
so might we stay nearby you, you good ones affording all possessions, in your midst.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Most interpr. take m├бdhya ─Б╠Бas indicating тАЬin the midst (of the shelter)тАЭ (ch├бrdiс╕е, of p─Бda b). This is certainly possible, though I weakly prefer my own rendering.

Griffith

Or, Asuras, when ye have sheltered the worshipper who goes to sacrifice, at eve
may we, O Vasus, ye possessors of all wealth, come then into the midst of You.

Geldner

Oder wenn ihr Asura┬┤s am Abend ├╝ber den rechtwandelnden Opferer euren Schirm haltet, so wollen wir, ihr Gute, Allwissende, mitten unter diesen Schirm von euch treten.

Grassmann

Wenn in der D├дmmrung, G├╢tter, ihr habt Schutz gereicht dem Frommen, der zum Opfer geht, So lasst in diesen euren Schirm uns treten ein, o gute, o allwissende.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬ(Gods), who are possessed of all wealth, bestow the desired (opulence) upon the intelligent Manu,offering oblations to you at sunrise, mid-day and sunset.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Connecting this to the next с╣Ыca: since you give thedesired (opulence) to Manu, therefore, we solicit of you…

Jamison Brereton

Since today when the sun rose, since at midday, since at the (time of) covering [=evening?],
you establish a thing of value for Manu the discerning oblator, o you affording all possessions,
1088 VIII.28тАУ29

Jamison Brereton Notes

The hapax ─Бt├║c- is difficult. See EWA s.v. Mostly for contextual reasons it is generally taken as referring to evening or night, and it has been connected to tv├бc- тАШskinтАЩ, with the sense of тАШcovering overтАЩ. I have followed this interpr., though with full awareness of how fragile it is. For one thing тАШcover as if with skinтАЩ (which must be the presumed semantic channel, one way or another) is not an altogether compelling way to get to тАШeveningтАЩ. For another, tv├бc- тАШskinтАЩ has no zero-grade forms.

Scarlatta (182-83) discusses several possibilities. Besides the тАШcoveringтАЩ hypothesis, he suggests, citing Schindler and K├╝mmel, that tv├бc- may belong with a root тИЪ*tuek╠п тАШsichtbar werdenтАЩ to which ─Бt├║c- could also belong, and that ─Бt├║c- might better be taken as an adj. with madhy├бс╣Гdine тАЬwhen midday is clearly visible.тАЭ He is less disturbed than I am that this would leave the verse without a third temporal period; furthermore, given that midday is the most тАЬclearly visibleтАЭ of the three standard time periods, it seems unnecessary to mark it as such. Another problem with ─Бt├║c- is that one is reluctant to separate it from the dat. tuc├й тАШfor progenyтАЩ in 14c. However, it is difficult to connect them and still maintain sensible semantics in our verse. Scarlatta makes a creative attempt: evening is the time when one goes back to oneтАЩs children, so тАШzu den Kindern hinтАЩ becomes тАШR├╝ckkehr nach HauseтАЩ. I admire the ingenuity but I think the unlikeliness speaks for itself.

Griffith

If ye to-day at sunrise, or at noon, or in the gloom of eve,
Lords of all riches, give fair treasure to the man, the wise man who hath sacrificed,

рд╣реЗ рд╕рдореНрд░рд╛рдЬрдГ рд╕рдореНрдпрдЧреНрджреАрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░реЛ рди ред рдПрдХрд╡рдЪрдирдВ рдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕рдореН ред рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛ рдЗрд╡ рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд╛рдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛ рдпрдерд╛ рдкрд┐рддреГрднрд┐рдГ рдкреЛрд╖реНрдпрд╛рд╕реНрддрджреНрд╡рджреНрдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдкреЛрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╡рдпрдореН ред рдмрд╣реБрдкрд╛рдпреНрдпрдВ рдмрд╣реБрднрд┐рд░реНрднреЛрдЬреНрдп рд╡рдГ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорддреНрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐ рддрддреН рдзрдирдореН рдЕрд╢реНрдпрд╛рдо рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рдо ред рдпреЗрди рдзрдиреЗрди рд╡рд╕реНрдпрдГ рд╡рд╕реАрдпреЛрд╜рддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рд╡рд╕реБрдорддреНрд╡рдореН рдЕрдирд╢рд╛рдорд╣реИ рдЕрд╢реНрдирд╡рд╛рдорд╣реИ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдордГ рее рдЕрд╢реНрдиреЛрддреЗрд░реНрд▓реЛрдЯрд┐ рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрди рд╢реНрдирдореНрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ рее рее рейрек рее

Wilson

better (state), o ─Аdityas.
